<review>This Goodwill is located in a somewhat dead shopping complex, I almost didn't find it because I thought it was out of business, but its hiding in there.
This store is medium to large for the average Goodwill, its relatively clean and relatively nicely laid out, but its not as nice as the store closer to the Los Angeles area.
This store had a medium sized section of books, CD's and DVD's and I found an amazing deal in the CD section.
The electronics section is on the small size and it was one of the least organized of the stores I have visited throughout Southern California.
The furniture area and selection was the smallest of any Goodwill I have visited.
The household items consisted of several rows and was on the small size.
Lots of clothing and shoes.
Despite being basically out in the middle of no-where's land - I enjoyed this store, it reminded me of the mid-west and I found both shoppers and employees friendly and even a bit entertaining.
I will visit this store again, on my return trips from the Ontario Headquarters.<//review><pictures>None</pictures>< response>

<name>Lucie N<//name><time>1503391715169< /time>< Rating>
4< /Rating>
<Review>This place is located in a large plaza with Chase Bank, Lee's Sandwiches, and El Super. There is plenty of parking but most likely not right in front since it is next to a banquet hall which is usually paid ked for receptions on weekends. The place can accommodate more than 95 seats and has 4 large tables for bigger groups. They leave the left side of the dining area for large groups. It has a bar area and a small stage with mic and keyboard. The menu has a little of everything. We came on a Saturday night and there was only two other tables there. However within 30 minutes, the pace filled up with many families with small children. The dining area and restrooms are clean. We ordered the Vietnamese crepe, Ha Noi noodles, and green papaya beef salad. The crepe was moderate size with adequate filling. However, it only comes with 3 types of vegetables to wrap (lettuce, mint, and beefsteak or perilla.) Usually most places that serve the crepe have a minimum of 5 vegetables. The papaya salad was generous and had two types of jerky and liver. It was very filling. The Ha Noi noodles only had two types of pork (grilled pork and pork patties) and same standard vegetables. It was still flavourful. The Vietnamese coffee was good here but not as strong compared to Lee's. All non Vietnamese people around us ordered Pho while the Vietnamese tables ordered various items. The servers were attentive. This place would receive a 5 star if not for vegetables and meager meat servings for the noodles. Also I haven't tried some of their more popular items like Pho to give them a higher rating. They do accept credit card and you can beat the hassle of crowded Vietnamese restaurants like in the Little Saigon area.< /Review>< Pictures>
None</Pictures>

< review>
Great sound system and a good room for mid-size club shows. The drawback is the terrible light setup. That is, great for dancing, not so much for focusing on a performer during a live show.

It's a deep stage and almost all the lights are behind the artist. The ones that do hit them from the front are generally overhead and hard. The result is generally a backlit performer unless they jump back deeper into the stage.

Another byproduct of this setup is that lights behind the artist focused on them tend to just aim straight into the eyes of the audience. Again, great for the dance portions of the evening. Frustrating during a performance.< /review>

< text>
We ordered for take out and it was ready at the expected pick up time. The pick up was quick and easy! They give you bread, which was amazing. I like how they put sea salt flakes on top of the bread, gives it extra flavor. We ordered the pesto with burrata, black truffle and lasagna. The black truffle sauce was amazing, super umami flavor. I suggest pairing it with tagliatelle instead of pappardelle for more bang for your buck. The pesto was an okay pesto, not memorable. The lasagna was flavorful, creamy and noodles were cooked pefectly. It held up great for the next day too. Overall, the food was good and they use high quality ingredients.</text>

<Pics>None</Pics>< review>
Street parking is kind of tricky, but I also make out okay. You should be able to find something no more than a block away. Dub nights and funky sole are fun. Drink prices are steep, but the covers are usually pretty low. Like $5-10, maybe $20 if there's a show. Two dance areas and a patio downstairs. Upstairs is a big spacious venue with a papi as well. I've never had a bad time here. Always fun and the people are friendly. Bathrooms are decent - for this type of venue. Dress code is casual - meaning you don't have to wear heels, and a ball gown, but you absolutely can. Stunting is optional here, but always welcome. And they've got two boots pizzeria next door to fill your drunken belly.</review>

<Response>None</Response>< text>
Came here for 143 and I was super hesitant because of all the mixed reviews. I came on the night that 88rising sponsored the event. My friend who was flying for 88rising told me the line was getting really long at about 8:30pm. My boyfriend and I were debating about driving or ubering over. We ended up ubering but later found there was valet parking across the street for about 20 bucks. We got there at about 9:30 and though there was a line, it didn't take us longer than 15-20 minutes to get in. The line was moving fast and it was $10 at the door to get in.

Once we got inside, it was like a mini reunion. Saw some old friends and people I knew from HS or even college. They have two stages with two different types of music playing--one upstairs and one downstairs. They have one bar upstairs and two downstairs and while their menu's are pretty similar, they may have different beer selections at the different bars. Beers start from like $5 and go up to about $9. They also sell food such as pizza for $5 a slice.

Protip: I wouldn't wear a nice purse or shoes as it's really easy to spill drinks in there. And, dress casual cute, honestly, if you don't need a purse, don't take it.

All in all, I was pleasantly surprised. The surprise guest for the night were Rich Brian and Niki. (They only played like two-ish songs but who cares! It was fun)

Once your drunk self wants to leave, they sell tacos and street dogs right outside the venue so you can grab one prior to ubering yourself home.< /text>

<user_id>105650960754729728153</user_id>< text>
This place is pretty fun. The layout inside is good. The stage has an area in front where you can dance, and there is lots of open space. There are two bars (one close to the stage and one farther away). The pillars all have little table things which means there are some places to set your stuff down, and the long sides of the room have couches.
The drink prices are not bad. A pint of pbr is 5 bucks, a pint of bud is 6, and Angel city brewery beers were 7/8.
The security is usually pretty chill. The one thing that annoys me is that they have that dude in the bathroom that holds all the paper towels so when you wash your hands you are forced to interact with him and feel guilty about not buying stuff from him. I can grab my own paper towels, I don't need to accept one from someone else.<//text>

1. One sentence review ‚Äì one of my favorite places to see shows in LA
2. The venue ‚Äì the Echoplex (downstairs) is larger than the Echo (upstairs), but both are pretty small venues that create a more intimate setting and leave no bad seat (spot) in the house. I‚Äôve never seen a show at either venue where I felt like I had a bad spot in the crowd.
3. Smoking ‚Äì the Echoplex has a separate side patio for smoking that‚Äôs really convenient and a nice place to hang out for a bit if you need a break between acts. They somewhat monitor for people blazing but I‚Äôve seen people get away with it pretty easily.
4. Parking ‚Äì the biggest downside is that the parking situation is really rough unless you get there early enough to get one of the spots in the two lots behind the venue.<//Text>
